We have been informed that international students here at Texas A&M University have been affected by these scams. ISS would like to remind students to be cautious when they are contacted by someone claiming to be from USCIS, DHS, or other such entities by phone.  U.S. Government offices will NOT contact you by phone asking for money, bank information, credit card information, social security numbers, or other personal information. \n\nThese scammers can be very savvy and even intimidating; they may threaten you with deportation, or other types of incarceration. Please do not allow yourself to be unsettled by the scammer\u2019s threats.  If you are contacted by someone stating that they represent a U.S. Government office or law enforcement please ask for their name, their badge number (if they claim to be an officer), and a phone number.  Do not give them any personal or financial information over the phone.   ISS advises you to also look at your caller ID and to write that number down as well.  If you are contacted by such a scammer do not attempt to address this alone, please come to the ISS Office, so that we can assist you. \n\n Sincerely,\n International Student Services"}
